<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Hurricane Irma</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"><div class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_notsynced plainlinks noprint nomobile" id="mw-fr-revisiontag"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><img alt="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page." class="flaggedrevs-icon" src="/w/extensions/FlaggedRevs/frontend/modules/img/doc-magnify.png" title="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page."/><img alt="show/hide details" class="fr-toggle-arrow" id="mw-fr-revisiontoggle" src="/w/extensions/FlaggedRevs/frontend/modules/img/arrow-down.png" style="display:none;"/></div>

<p><b>Hurricane Irma</b> was an extremely powerful and catastrophic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Verde-type_hurricane" title="Cape Verde-type hurricane">Cape Verde-type hurricane</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Atlantic_hurricane_records#Intensity" title="List of Atlantic hurricane records">strongest</a> observed in the Atlantic since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Wilma</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a> in terms of maximum sustained winds. It was the first Category 5 hurricane to strike the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a> on record, followed by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> only two weeks later. It was also the most intense Atlantic hurricane to strike the United States since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Katrina</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>, and the first major hurricane to make landfall in <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Wilma</a> in 2005. The ninth <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">named storm</a>, fourth <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">hurricane</a>, and second <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale#Categories" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">major hurricane</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">2017 Atlantic hurricane season</a>, Irma caused widespread and catastrophic damage throughout its long lifetime, particularly in parts of the northeastern <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a>.</p>
<p>Irma developed on August 30, 2017 near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_Islands" title="Cape Verde Islands">Cape Verde Islands</a>, from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> that had moved off the west African coast three days prior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Under favorable conditions, Irma <a href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">rapidly intensified</a> shortly after formation, becoming a Category 2 hurricane on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Saffir–Simpson scale</a> within a mere 24 hours. It became a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Category_3_hurricane" title="Category 3 hurricane">Category 3 hurricane</a> (and therefore a major hurricane) shortly afterward; however, the intensity fluctuated between Categories 2 and 3 for the next several days due to a series of <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycles</a>. On September 4, Irma resumed intensifying, becoming a Category 5 hurricane by early the next day. On September 6, Irma reached its peak intensity with 185 mph (295 km/h) winds and a minimum <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">pressure</a> of 914 hPa (27.0 inHg), making it the second most intense tropical cyclone worldwide so far in 2017, behind only <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a>, and the strongest worldwide in 2017 in terms of wind speed. Another eyewall replacement cycle caused Irma to weaken back to a Category 4 hurricane, but the storm attained Category 5 status for a second time before making landfall in Cuba. After dropping to Category 3 intensity due to land interaction, the storm re-intensified to Category 4 status as it crossed warm waters between Cuba and Florida, before making landfall on <a href="/wiki/Cudjoe_Key,_Florida" title="Cudjoe Key, Florida">Cudjoe Key</a> with maximum sustained winds at 130 mph (215 km/h). Irma dropped back to Category 3 by the time it made a second Florida landfall on <a href="/wiki/Marco_Island,_Florida" title="Marco Island, Florida">Marco Island</a>. Irma weakened to a Category 2 hurricane later that day, the first time it weakened below major hurricane status in over a week, and eventually dissipated off the coast of <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> on September 16.</p>
<p>The storm caused catastrophic damage in <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Saint Barthélemy">Saint Barthélemy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands</a> as a Category 5 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> As of September 30, the hurricane has caused at least 132 deaths: one in <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>, one in <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, three in <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a>, four in the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>, 10 in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, 11 in the <a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a>, one in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, three in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, four on the Dutch side of <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>, 88 in the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous United States</a>, four in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</a>, and two others in unknown locations in the Caribbean.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">Meteorological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Irma_2017_track.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Irma_2017_track.png/300px-Irma_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Irma_2017_track.png/450px-Irma_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Irma_2017_track.png/600px-Irma_2017_track.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Irma_2017_track.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map plotting the track and intensity of the storm, according to the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Saffir–Simpson scale</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> (NHC) began monitoring a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> over western Africa on August 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> This wave moved off the coast of the continent late on August 27. Throughout the next two days, showers and thunderstorms associated with the wave became better organized and gradually coalesced into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">low pressure area</a>, as the system passed just south of and then through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_Islands" title="Cape Verde Islands">Cape Verde Islands</a> on August 29,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> with the NHC stating that any significant organization of the disturbance would result in the classification of a tropical depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Further organization over the next 24 hours or so led to classification of the disturbance as Tropical Storm Irma, at 15:00 UTC on August 30, based on <a href="/wiki/Scatterometer" title="Scatterometer">scatterometer</a> data and <a href="/wiki/Dvorak_technique" title="Dvorak technique">satellite estimates</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> With warm <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperatures</a> and low wind shear, strengthening was anticipated, with the only hindrance being slightly cooler waters and drier air.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Irma_2017-09-03_1545Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2432" data-file-width="3680" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Irma_2017-09-03_1545Z.jpg/220px-Irma_2017-09-03_1545Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Irma_2017-09-03_1545Z.jpg/330px-Irma_2017-09-03_1545Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Irma_2017-09-03_1545Z.jpg/440px-Irma_2017-09-03_1545Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Irma_2017-09-03_1545Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Visible_Infrared_Imaging_Radiometer_Suite" title="Visible Infrared Imaging Radiometer Suite">VIIRS</a> satellite image of Hurricane Irma on September 3</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The nascent storm began developing upper-level poleward <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Anticyclone" title="Anticyclone">anticyclone</a> became established over the system, with <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">banding features</a> becoming increasingly evident in satellite images.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Early on August 31, shortly after the development of a <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a> (CDO) and an <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye feature</a>, Irma <a href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">rapidly intensified</a> beginning at 09:00 UTC on August 31, with winds increasing from 70 mph (110 km/h) to 115 mph (185 km/h) in only 12 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> On September 2, a ship passed 60 mi (90 km) to the west of the center of Irma, recording maximum winds of 45 mph (70 km/h), which indicated that the eye of Irma remained compact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> A strengthening subtropical ridge over the central North Atlantic pushed Irma from a western to southwestern direction on September 2 and 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHC_discussion_17_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHC_discussion_17-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_hunters" title="Hurricane hunters">aircraft reconnaissance mission</a> departed from <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> on the afternoon of September 3, discovering an eye 29 mi (47 km) in diameter and surface winds of 115 mph (185 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHC_discussion_17_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-NHC_discussion_17-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Irma_5_September_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_view.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Hurricane_Irma_5_September_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_view.gif/220px-Hurricane_Irma_5_September_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_view.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Hurricane_Irma_5_September_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_view.gif/330px-Hurricane_Irma_5_September_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_view.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Hurricane_Irma_5_September_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_view.gif/440px-Hurricane_Irma_5_September_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_view.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Irma_5_September_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_view.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Infrared loop of Hurricane Irma approaching the northern Leeward Islands on September 5, around the time of its upgrade to a Category 5 hurricane</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On September 4, after moving into more favorable conditions, Irma strengthened into a Category 4 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> As it continued approaching the Leeward Islands, Irma underwent a second and more robust period of rapid intensification, becoming a Category 5 hurricane by 11:45 UTC on the following day, with winds of 175 mph (280 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-20">[20]</a></sup> As it began to take on <a href="/wiki/Annular_tropical_cyclone" title="Annular tropical cyclone">annular characteristics</a>, the extremely powerful hurricane continued to intensify,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> with maximum sustained winds peaking at 185 mph (295 km/h) near 00:00 UTC on September 6 – which would remain steady and unchanged for the next 37 hours. Six hours later, Irma made landfall along the northern coast of <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a> near peak strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Later that day, around 21:00 UTC, the storm's pressure bottomed out at 914 hPa (27.0 inHg) – this was the lowest in the Atlantic since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dean" title="Hurricane Dean">Dean</a> in 2007. While maintaining its intensity, Irma made successive landfalls at approximately 12:00 UTC on <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>, and at 17:00 UTC on <a href="/wiki/Ginger_Island" title="Ginger Island">Ginger Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tortola" title="Tortola">Tortola</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NASA_Hot_water_ahead_for_Hurricane_Irma.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="581" data-file-width="768" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/NASA_Hot_water_ahead_for_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/220px-NASA_Hot_water_ahead_for_Hurricane_Irma.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/NASA_Hot_water_ahead_for_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/330px-NASA_Hot_water_ahead_for_Hurricane_Irma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/NASA_Hot_water_ahead_for_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/440px-NASA_Hot_water_ahead_for_Hurricane_Irma.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NASA_Hot_water_ahead_for_Hurricane_Irma.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sea surface temperatures in Hurricane Irma's path.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Shortly before 06:00 UTC on September 8, Irma made landfall on the Bahamian island <a href="/wiki/Little_Inagua" title="Little Inagua">Little Inagua</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWC_Irma_track_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWC_Irma_track-23">[23]</a></sup> About three hours later, an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a> caused Irma to weaken to a Category 4 hurricane, but the storm regained Category 5 status 18 hours later before making landfall in Cuba. After weakening to a Category 3 due to land interaction with Cuba, Irma reintensified into a Category 4 hurricane while crossing over the <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Florida" title="Straits of Florida">Straits of Florida</a>. At 13:10 UTC on September 10, Irma made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Cudjoe_Key,_Florida" title="Cudjoe Key, Florida">Cudjoe Key, Florida</a> with maximum sustained winds of 130 mph (215 km/h) and a central pressure of 929 hPa (27.4 inHg).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Later that day, at 19:35 UTC, Irma made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Marco_Island,_Florida" title="Marco Island, Florida">Marco Island</a> with maximum sustained winds of 115 mph (185 km/h) and a central pressure of 940 hPa (28 inHg); the Marco Island Police Department recorded a wind gust of 130 mph (215 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naples,_FL" title="Naples, FL">Naples, FL</a> Municipal Airport measured wind gusts up to 142 mph (229 km/h). About a half an hour later, Irma made landfall in Naples at the same intensity. Irma weakened into a Category 2 storm once inland, and below hurricane intensity at 12:00 UTC on September 11. At 03:00 UTC on September 12, Irma weakened to a tropical depression over the Georgia-Alabama border, and degenerated into a post-tropical low about 24 hours later north of <a href="/wiki/Tupelo,_Mississippi" title="Tupelo, Mississippi">Tupelo, Mississippi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Irma's remnants continued moving towards the northwest over the next day, before turning northward and then accelerating to the northeast on September 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPC_weather_map_on_Sep_14_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-WPC_weather_map_on_Sep_14-27">[27]</a></sup> Early on September 15, Irma's remnants began moving off the New England coastline, becoming increasingly disorganized while continuing to weaken. Later on the same day, Irma's remnants began interacting with a cold front stretching over <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPC_weather_map_on_Sep_15_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-WPC_weather_map_on_Sep_15-28">[28]</a></sup> On September 16, Irma's remnant circulation collapsed, and the majority of Irma's remnant moisture was absorbed into <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Hurricane Jose</a> later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPC_weather_map_on_Sep_16_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-WPC_weather_map_on_Sep_16-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Data collected by NASA showed that ocean surface temperatures in the path of Irma were above 30 °C (86 °F) at the time, more than enough to sustain a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Category_5_hurricane" title="Category 5 hurricane">Category 5 hurricane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Additionally, ocean surface temperatures in areas between Cuba and south Florida extended to 32 °C (90 °F),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scary_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-scary-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-change_strength_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-change_strength-32">[32]</a></sup> which could support a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maximum_potential_intensity" title="Maximum potential intensity">maximum potential intensity</a> of 200 miles per hour (320 km/h), if ideal conditions had been met.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-impossible_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-impossible-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparations">Preparations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Preparations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Caribbean">Caribbean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Caribbean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Given that Irma's forecast track was along much of the Caribbean island chain, hurricane warnings were issued for the northern Leeward Islands, Puerto Rico and parts of Hispaniola on September 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 4, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> declared a state of emergency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> By September 6, the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> had deployed response teams in Puerto Rico and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a>. Supplies, including food rations, medical supplies, and blankets, were pre-staged in strategic locations on the islands for distribution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, residents safeguarded their homes and cleaned up their properties in anticipation of strong winds. Emergency crews were put on standby at public shelters and hospitals by September 5 to assist with any evacuations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Expecting a direct hit, more than half of the residents on Barbuda took shelter,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-38">[38]</a></sup> and relief supplies were preemptively mobilized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Guadeloupe, low-lying and cliff-edge homes were evacuated at the threat of flooding and erosion. Schools and public businesses closed on September 5 and 6. Hospitals stocked up on three days' worth of supplies and checked the functionality of their generators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Of the island's 32 municipalities, 22 activated their emergency plans; 1,500 people were urged to take shelter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guadeloupe_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupe-42">[42]</a></sup> The island sustained relatively minor damage and became the base for relief efforts on St. Martin (<a href="/wiki/Collectivity_of_Saint_Martin" title="Collectivity of Saint Martin">Collectivity of Saint Martin</a>) and St. Barts (<a href="/wiki/Saint_Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Saint Barthélemy">Saint Barthélemy</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Though the core of the hurricane was expected to remain north of the island, a yellow alert was issued for <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> due to the likelihood of rough seas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The island dispatched relief supplies and military reinforcements to its neighboring islands of <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Saint Barthélemy">Saint Barthélemy</a>, who faced a greater risk of a direct impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The National Emergency Management Organization on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a> urged small craft operators and swimmers to be mindful of forecasts for high surf.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Small Craft Warnings and High Surf Advisories were hoisted for <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, where residents were urged to remain vigilant of the potential for high waves, landslides, and flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos" title="Turks and Caicos">Turks and Caicos</a>, evacuation orders were issued for low-lying areas starting September 5. Schools were closed, government buildings were boarded up, and shelters were opened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Officials spread warnings to residents in English, Creole, and Spanish via social media, radio, SMS text, and <a href="/wiki/WhatsApp" title="WhatsApp">WhatsApp</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 5, the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> activated the <a href="/wiki/International_Charter_on_Space_and_Major_Disasters" title="International Charter on Space and Major Disasters">International Charter on Space and Major Disasters</a>, thus providing for humanitarian satellite coverage;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hurricane_Irma_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hurricane_Irma-50">[50]</a></sup> the United States and Haiti followed suit two days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S._Activates_International_Charter_on_Space_and_Major_Disasters_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._Activates_International_Charter_on_Space_and_Major_Disasters-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> According to officials, 11,200 people were evacuated from vulnerable areas prior to the storm's arrival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JamObsHelp_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-JamObsHelp-53">[53]</a></sup> 7,400 tourists were moved to <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a>, away from beach resorts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOLA_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOLA-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, government officials and aid organizations struggled with early preparation and evacuation efforts. While some officials blamed reluctance and indifference on the part of the population, others "admitted they were not prepared for the onslaught and no mandatory evacuation orders were in place ahead of Irma's approach," per <i>The Guardian</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOLA_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOLA-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islands_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-islands-55">[55]</a></sup> Local officials contended that they had not received promised funds, supplies, or equipment from the national government. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Stabilization_Mission_in_Haiti" title="United Nations Stabilization Mission in Haiti">United Nations Stabilization Mission in Haiti</a> prepared its 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeepers</a> and engineers to assist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a>, the government began preparations the week prior to the hurricane's arrival, including securing national sports facilities to use as shelters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> By September 7, the government had evacuated 1,609 people by air from the southern islands, including 365 from <a href="/wiki/Bimini" title="Bimini">Bimini</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Controlled cutting of the power supply to southern and central Bahamian islands was conducted in advance of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Shelters were made available, though usage was low due to most evacuees staying with family on other islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Of the 2,679 foreign tourists still in The Bahamas on September 7, about 1,200 were being housed at <a href="/wiki/Atlantis_Paradise_Island" title="Atlantis Paradise Island">Atlantis Paradise Island</a>, one of the most hurricane-ready structures in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, meteorologists did not initially predict a direct hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT9_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT9-62">[62]</a></sup> Fuel conservation was enacted in <a href="/wiki/Camag%C3%BCey_Province" title="Camagüey Province">Camagüey Province</a> to ensure that enough would be available during post-storm power outages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The Civil Defense evacuated nearly one million people from low-lying areas, including thousands of Canadian and European tourists in the <a href="/wiki/Jardines_del_Rey" title="Jardines del Rey">Jardines del Rey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT9_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT9-62">[62]</a></sup> Dolphins at a <a href="/wiki/Cayo_Guillermo" title="Cayo Guillermo">Cayo Guillermo</a> resort were evacuated by helicopter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT9_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-NYT9-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainland_United_States">Mainland United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mainland United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida">Florida</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Florida">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:220px;" videopayload='&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:852px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Florida_Governor_Rick_Scott_on_Evacuations.webmsd.webm/852px--Florida_Governor_Rick_Scott_on_Evacuations.webmsd.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:852px;height:480px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="34.343" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Florida_Governor_Rick_Scott_on_Evacuations.webmsd.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b2/Florida_Governor_Rick_Scott_on_Evacuations.webmsd.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="Small WebM (240P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 240P" data-transcodekey="240p.webm" data-width="426" data-height="240" data-bandwidth="321840" data-framerate="25"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/b2/Florida_Governor_Rick_Scott_on_Evacuations.webmsd.webm/Florida_Governor_Rick_Scott_on_Evacuations.webmsd.webm.360p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="WebM (360P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="640" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="568336" data-framerate="25"/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;'><img alt="File:Florida Governor Rick Scott on Evacuations.webmsd.webm" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Florida_Governor_Rick_Scott_on_Evacuations.webmsd.webm/220px--Florida_Governor_Rick_Scott_on_Evacuations.webmsd.webm.jpg" style="width:220px;height:124px"/><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b2/Florida_Governor_Rick_Scott_on_Evacuations.webmsd.webm" target="new" title="Play media"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Florida_Governor_Rick_Scott_on_Evacuations.webmsd.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
'Florida Governor <a href="/wiki/Rick_Scott" title="Rick Scott">Rick Scott</a> on Evacuations' video from <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">Voice of America</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On September 4, Florida Governor <a href="/wiki/Rick_Scott" title="Rick Scott">Rick Scott</a> declared a state of emergency for Florida,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> and placed 100 members of the <a href="/wiki/Florida_National_Guard" title="Florida National Guard">Florida National Guard</a> on duty to assist in preparations. All 7,000 troops were ordered to be on duty by September 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Officials advised residents to stock their hurricane kits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Governor Scott suspended tolls on all toll roads in Florida, including <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_Turnpike" title="Florida's Turnpike">Florida's Turnpike</a>, starting at 5:00 p.m. on September 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> All state offices in Florida were closed on September 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> All schools in the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a> were ordered closed from September 6 until further notice. Mandatory evacuations for the islands were expected, with tourists to leave on September 6 and residents the following day; an estimated 25% of residents stayed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doublepunch_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-doublepunch-71">[71]</a></sup> Schools and colleges were closed in 44 of the state's 67 counties, before Governor Scott ordered all state colleges, universities, schools, and offices to be closed from September 8 to 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 6, the mayor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale" title="Fort Lauderdale">Fort Lauderdale</a> ordered mandatory evacuations for all residents east of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_1" title="US 1">US 1</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_Alvare_Santora_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Alvare_Santora-73">[73]</a></sup> The city of <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa</a>, on the west coast of Florida, declared a local state of emergency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Central_Florida" title="University of Central Florida">University of Central Florida</a> canceled classes from September 7 to 17, and its Orlando campuses closed from September 8 to 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Shelters were opened in the following counties: <a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">Broward</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flagler_County,_Florida" title="Flagler County, Florida">Flagler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hardee_County,_Florida" title="Hardee County, Florida">Hardee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hendry_County,_Florida" title="Hendry County, Florida">Hendry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_County,_Florida" title="Hillsborough County, Florida">Hillsborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manatee_County,_Florida" title="Manatee County, Florida">Manatee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marion_County,_Florida" title="Marion County, Florida">Marion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">Miami-Dade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_Florida" title="Orange County, Florida">Orange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_County,_Florida" title="Palm Beach County, Florida">Palm Beach</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pasco_County,_Florida" title="Pasco County, Florida">Pasco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pinellas_County,_Florida" title="Pinellas County, Florida">Pinellas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brevard_County,_Florida" title="Brevard County, Florida">Brevard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brevard_County,_Florida" title="Brevard County, Florida">Brevard</a> has 3 types of shelters: pet friendly, general population, and special needs. While not every shelter opens for every emergency, there were four pet friendly shelters, 11 general population shelters, and five special needs shelters which were not advertised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> A special needs shelter "provides more care and supervision than a general shelter to help meet your special needs during an evacuation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Irma_2017_Doral_preparations.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Hurricane_Irma_2017_Doral_preparations.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Irma_2017_Doral_preparations.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Hurricane_Irma_2017_Doral_preparations.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Irma_2017_Doral_preparations.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Hurricane_Irma_2017_Doral_preparations.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Irma_2017_Doral_preparations.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Irma_2017_Doral_preparations.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Residents in <a href="/wiki/Doral,_Florida" title="Doral, Florida">Doral</a> installing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_shutters" title="Hurricane shutters">hurricane shutters</a> in advance of the storm</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At around 15:00 UTC on September 7, a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">hurricane watch</a> was issued for parts of South Florida, from the <a href="/wiki/Jupiter,_Florida" title="Jupiter, Florida">Jupiter Inlet</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bonita_Beach,_Florida" title="Bonita Beach, Florida">Bonita Beach</a>, including the Florida Keys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> At 02:00 UTC, Friday September 8, a hurricane warning was issued for the Florida Keys, extending as far north as Miami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> As of 00:51 UTC September 8, the governor ordered all public schools and colleges statewide to be closed Friday and Monday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Most commercial airports, including <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport" title="Fort Lauderdale–Hollywood International Airport">Fort Lauderdale–Hollywood International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami International Airport</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Orlando_International_Airport" title="Orlando International Airport">Orlando International Airport</a>, ceased commercial operations by late Saturday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a> was predicted at 10 to 15 ft at <a href="/wiki/Cape_Sable" title="Cape Sable">Florida's southern tip</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> and above 9 feet along the west coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the fifth time in its 45-year history, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World_Resort" title="Walt Disney World Resort">Walt Disney World Resort</a> was completely closed due to the storm. Its theme parks, water parks, and <a href="/wiki/Disney_Springs" title="Disney Springs">Disney Springs</a> were all closed by 9:00 pm on September 9. Due to Hurricane Irma, the parks did not open on September 10 or 11. Other <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando</a>-area theme parks, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_Orlando_Resort" title="Universal Orlando Resort">Universal Orlando Resort</a> and <a href="/wiki/SeaWorld_Orlando" title="SeaWorld Orlando">SeaWorld Orlando</a>, were also closed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">Kennedy Space Center</a> closed until September 13, and sustained the storm with minor damage. However the space center is currently without water utilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the evening of September 8, hundreds of thousands of Floridians had evacuated, making it the largest evacuation in the state's history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_Alvare_Santora_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Alvare_Santora-73">[73]</a></sup> Evacuees caused significant traffic congestion on northbound <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Florida" title="Interstate 95 in Florida">Interstate 95</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_75_in_Florida" title="Interstate 75 in Florida">Interstate 75</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_Turnpike" title="Florida's Turnpike">Florida's Turnpike</a>, exacerbated by the fact that the entire Florida peninsula was within the cone of uncertainty in the National Hurricane Center's forecast path in the days before the storm, so evacuees from both coasts headed north, as evacuees would not be safer by fleeing to the opposite coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slate_Mak_8_September_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slate_Mak_8_September-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_Fla_evacuations_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Fla_evacuations-91">[91]</a></sup> Fuel was in short supply throughout peninsular Florida during the week before Irma's arrival, especially along evacuation routes, leading to hours-long lines at fuel stations and even escorts of fuel trucks by the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Highway_Patrol" title="Florida Highway Patrol">Florida Highway Patrol</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slate_Mak_8_September_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-Slate_Mak_8_September-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_Fla_evacuations_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Fla_evacuations-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fla_Gov_preparedness_statement_5_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fla_Gov_preparedness_statement_5-92">[92]</a></sup> Use of the left <a href="/wiki/Shoulder_(road)" title="Shoulder (road)">shoulder</a> as a lane for moving traffic was allowed on northbound Interstate 75 from <a href="/wiki/Wildwood,_Florida" title="Wildwood, Florida">Wildwood</a> to the Georgia state line (about 150 miles/​250 km) beginning September 8 and on eastbound <a href="/wiki/Interstate_4" title="Interstate 4">Interstate 4</a> from Tampa to <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_429" title="Florida State Road 429">State Road 429</a> near <a href="/wiki/Celebration,_Florida" title="Celebration, Florida">Celebration</a> for a few hours on September 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OS_I-75_shoulder_use_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-OS_I-75_shoulder_use-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OS_I-4_shoulder_use_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-OS_I-4_shoulder_use-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWC_airport_closures_and_shoulder_use_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWC_airport_closures_and_shoulder_use-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WFLA_9_September_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-WFLA_9_September-96">[96]</a></sup> It was the first time that the shoulder-use plan, which was introduced at the start of the 2017 hurricane season, was implemented by the state for hurricane evacuations. The shoulder-use plan was implemented in place of labor- and resource-intensive <a href="/wiki/Contraflow_lane_reversal" title="Contraflow lane reversal">contraflow lane reversal</a>, in which both sides of an interstate highway are used for one direction of traffic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OS_May_2017_shoulder-use_plan_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-OS_May_2017_shoulder-use_plan-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OS_I-4_shoulder_use_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-OS_I-4_shoulder_use-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Officials from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="Environmental Protection Agency">Environmental Protection Agency</a>, which had been criticized for its response to <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Hurricane Harvey</a>, took special measures to inspect and secure hazardous materials, especially at <a href="/wiki/Superfund" title="Superfund">Superfund</a> sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Elsewhere">Elsewhere</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Elsewhere">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emergency_shoulder_use_Interstate_4_before_Hurricane_Irma_6.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Emergency_shoulder_use_Interstate_4_before_Hurricane_Irma_6.jpg/220px-Emergency_shoulder_use_Interstate_4_before_Hurricane_Irma_6.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Emergency_shoulder_use_Interstate_4_before_Hurricane_Irma_6.jpg/330px-Emergency_shoulder_use_Interstate_4_before_Hurricane_Irma_6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Emergency_shoulder_use_Interstate_4_before_Hurricane_Irma_6.jpg/440px-Emergency_shoulder_use_Interstate_4_before_Hurricane_Irma_6.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Emergency_shoulder_use_Interstate_4_before_Hurricane_Irma_6.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Eastbound Interstate 4 lanes on the afternoon of September 9 are filled with evacuating traffic from the Gulf Coast (note the <a href="/wiki/Shoulder_(road)#Emergency_use_by_all_traffic" title="Shoulder (road)">emergency shoulder use</a> by moving traffic), while westbound lanes are almost empty at 5 PM on a Saturday afternoon</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Georgia" title="Governor of Georgia">Georgia Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Deal" title="Nathan Deal">Nathan Deal</a> declared a state of emergency initially for all six coastal counties on September 6; however, the state of emergency was expanded to cover 30 counties in southeast and east central Georgia, and Governor Deal ordered mandatory evacuations for all areas east of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Georgia" title="Interstate 95 in Georgia">Interstate 95</a> on September 7. <a href="/wiki/Contraflow_lane_reversal" title="Contraflow lane reversal">Contraflow lane reversal</a> for <a href="/wiki/Interstate_16" title="Interstate 16">Interstate 16</a> took effect on September 9 at 8:00 a.m. from <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah</a> to <a href="/wiki/Dublin,_Georgia" title="Dublin, Georgia">Dublin, Georgia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GA_SOE_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-GA_SOE-99">[99]</a></sup> On September 8, Governor Deal further expanded the state of emergency to cover 94 counties south of the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_metropolitan_area" title="Atlanta metropolitan area">Atlanta metropolitan area</a>, with mandatory evacuations expanded to include the entirety of <a href="/wiki/Chatham_County,_Georgia" title="Chatham County, Georgia">Chatham County</a> as well as low-lying areas west of I-95.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GA_SOE_2_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-GA_SOE_2-100">[100]</a></sup> In total, 540,000 people on the Georgia coast were ordered to leave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian8_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian8-101">[101]</a></sup> On September 10, the state of emergency for Georgia was extended to cover the entire state, while <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> was placed under its first-ever tropical storm warning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GA_SOE_3_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-GA_SOE_3-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doublepunch_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-doublepunch-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>All <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgia_state_parks" title="Georgia state parks">Georgia state parks</a> were open for free to evacuees, as was the 800-acre camping area at <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Motor_Speedway" title="Atlanta Motor Speedway">Atlanta Motor Speedway</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whnt9617_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-whnt9617-103">[103]</a></sup> Reversible <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HOT_lane" title="HOT lane">HOT lanes</a> on <a href="/wiki/Interstate_75_in_Georgia" title="Interstate 75 in Georgia">Interstate 75 in Georgia</a> through south <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro_Atlanta" title="Metro Atlanta">metro Atlanta</a> were open 24 hours northbound with no tolls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Governor_of_North_Carolina" title="Governor of North Carolina">North Carolina Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Roy_Cooper" title="Roy Cooper">Roy Cooper</a> declared a state of emergency on September 6,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_South_Carolina" title="Governor of South Carolina">South Carolina Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Henry_McMaster" title="Henry McMaster">Henry McMaster</a> following suit the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Virginia" title="Governor of Virginia">Governor of Virginia</a> <a href="/wiki/Terry_McAuliffe" title="Terry McAuliffe">Terry McAuliffe</a> declared a state of emergency on September 8 in order to protect Virginia residents and to mobilize resources in support of neighboring states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Officials in <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> stated that there would not be much time for preparations if Irma failed to make the projected northward turn, but that South Texas or Florida would not be a good evacuation destination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Talladega_Superspeedway" title="Talladega Superspeedway">Talladega Superspeedway</a> near <a href="/wiki/Talladega,_Alabama" title="Talladega, Alabama">Talladega, Alabama</a>, opened their campgrounds to evacuees free of charge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whnt9617_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-whnt9617-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 10, 2017 Tennessee Governor <a href="/wiki/Bill_Haslam" title="Bill Haslam">Bill Haslam</a> issued an executive order allowing medical professionals in other states to practice in Tennessee to aid Hurricane Irma evacuees. This order also allowed pharmacies to give out 14-day supplies of medicine, and gave women and children from outside the state the ability to participate in the Tennessee Department of Health programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In professional sports, the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Dolphins" title="Miami Dolphins">Miami Dolphins</a>–<a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Buccaneers" title="Tampa Bay Buccaneers">Tampa Bay Buccaneers</a> game scheduled for September 10 at <a href="/wiki/Hard_Rock_Stadium" title="Hard Rock Stadium">Hard Rock Stadium</a> in Miami was postponed to November 19 due to the storm's threat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> had their September 11–13 series moved from <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Field" title="Tropicana Field">Tropicana Field</a> in St. Petersburg to <a href="/wiki/Citi_Field" title="Citi Field">Citi Field</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">Minor League Baseball</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_League" title="Florida State League">Florida State League</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carolina_League" title="Carolina League">Carolina League</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Southern_League_(baseball)" title="Southern League (baseball)">Southern League</a> called off their championship finals and as a result, named their division series winners league co-champions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Miami_FC" title="Miami FC">Miami FC</a> played a 3–3 tie with <a href="/wiki/New_York_Cosmos_(2010)" title="New York Cosmos (2010)">New York Cosmos</a> on September 7 at home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Their fixture at <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Deltas" title="San Francisco Deltas">San Francisco Deltas</a> on September 10 was cancelled so the players and staff could prepare for the storm with their families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Pride" title="Orlando Pride">Orlando Pride</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Women%27s_Soccer_League" title="National Women's Soccer League">National Women's Soccer League</a> rescheduled their September 9 match to September 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Orlando_City_SC" title="Orlando City SC">Orlando City SC</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a> did not have any scheduled home games in September, but was unable to return to training in Orlando due to Hurricane Irma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/2017_NCAA_Division_I_FBS_football_season" title="2017 NCAA Division I FBS football season">college football</a>, the <a href="/wiki/UCF_Knights" title="UCF Knights">UCF Knights</a>-<a href="/wiki/Memphis_Tigers" title="Memphis Tigers">Memphis Tigers</a> game set to take place at 20:00 EDT on September 9 was moved to September 30, replacing UCF's game against <a href="/wiki/2017_Maine_Black_Bears_football_team" title="2017 Maine Black Bears football team">Maine</a> and Memphis game against <a href="/wiki/2017_Georgia_State_Panthers_football_team" title="2017 Georgia State Panthers football team">Georgia State</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Memphis_Rescheduled_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Memphis_Rescheduled-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> after originally being moved up by 25.5 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> UCF also cancelled their game against <a href="/wiki/2017_Georgia_Tech_Yellow_Jackets_football_team" title="2017 Georgia Tech Yellow Jackets football team">Georgia Tech</a> originally scheduled for September 16, while <a href="/wiki/Spectrum_Stadium" title="Spectrum Stadium">UCF's stadium</a> hosted the National Guard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USF_Bulls" title="USF Bulls">USF Bulls</a>-<a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Huskies" title="Connecticut Huskies">Connecticut Huskies</a> football game was also cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Miami_Hurricanes_football" title="Miami Hurricanes football">Miami Hurricanes</a>–<a href="/wiki/Arkansas_State_University" title="Arkansas State University">Arkansas State Redwolves</a> game scheduled for September 9 at <a href="/wiki/Centennial_Bank_Stadium" title="Centennial Bank Stadium">Centennial Bank Stadium</a> in Arkansas was canceled due to travel concerns for the University of Miami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators" title="Florida Gators">Florida Gators</a>-<a href="/wiki/Northern_Colorado_Bears" title="Northern Colorado Bears">Northern Colorado Bears</a> match in Gainesville, originally scheduled for September 9 was cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Seminoles" title="Florida State Seminoles">Florida State Seminoles</a> contest against the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana%E2%80%93Monroe_Warhawks" title="Louisiana–Monroe Warhawks">Louisiana–Monroe Warhawks</a> was canceled on September 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> The Seminoles' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_State-Miami_football_rivalry" title="Florida State-Miami football rivalry">rivalry</a> game with the Hurricanes in Tallahassee, originally scheduled for the following Saturday, September 16, was postponed three weeks later to October 7. The <a href="/wiki/FIU_Panthers" title="FIU Panthers">FIU Panthers</a> game against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcorn_State_Braves" title="Alcorn State Braves">Alcorn State Braves</a> was moved up a day and relocated to <a href="/wiki/Legion_Field" title="Legion Field">Legion Field</a> in <a href="/wiki/Birmingham,_Alabama" title="Birmingham, Alabama">Birmingham, Alabama</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Southern_Eagles" title="Georgia Southern Eagles">Georgia Southern Eagles</a> game against the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Wildcats" title="New Hampshire Wildcats">New Hampshire Wildcats</a> on September 9 was also moved to Legion Field for that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="FEMA_funding">FEMA funding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: FEMA funding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As of September 5, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> (FEMA) funding was running dangerously low due to its response to <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Hurricane Harvey</a> in Texas the previous week, prompting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trump_administration" title="Trump administration">Trump administration</a> to request an immediate $8 billion in additional funding as Irma approached Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Given the rate that current funds are being consumed and the catastrophic damage, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a> almost doubled the requested amount to $15.3 billion, with the understanding that this would only be about 10% of what will be required for responding to Harvey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hurricane Irma's path was such that its impact was both far-reaching and devastating, with confirmed landfalls in <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos" title="Turks and Caicos">Turks and Caicos</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, and the United States. Furthermore, the size of the storm system meant that destruction was prevalent even in territories well removed from landfall occurrences.</p>

<td scope="row" style="text-align: left;">United States</td>
<td>88</td>
<td>&gt; <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7010500000000000000♠</span>$50 billion</td>
<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_AFP_death_toll_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_AFP_death_toll-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-costly_recovery_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-costly_recovery-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assess_damage_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-assess_damage-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></td>

<td scope="row" style="text-align: left;"><a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</a></td>
<td>4</td>
<td><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7009240000000000000♠</span>$2.4 billion</td>

<tr style="text-align:right;">
<td scope="row" style="text-align: left;">Unknown</td>
<td>2</td>
<td class="table-na" data-sort-value="" style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; vertical-align: middle; font-size: smaller; text-align: center;">N/A</td>
<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_death_toll_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_death_toll-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nuclear_landscape_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-nuclear_landscape-136">[136]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr class="sortbottom">
<th scope="row" style="text-align: left;">Totals:</th>
<th style="text-align:right;"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7002132000000000000♠</span>132</th>
<th style="text-align:right;">&gt; <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7010628650000000000♠</span>$62.9 billion</th>
<td></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The eyewall of the hurricane moved over <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a> near its record peak intensity during the night of September 5–6;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> a local anemometer reportedly measured an unofficial gust of 155 mph (250 km/h) before being blown away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Though some reports of structural damage such as blown off roofs surfaced shortly after,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> the exact state of the island remained unclear for hours after Irma's passage, as downed phone lines ceased all communication with nearby islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-38">[38]</a></sup> Later that afternoon, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Gaston_Browne" title="Gaston Browne">Gaston Browne</a> surveyed the territory by helicopter, revealing an effectively uninhabitable island. Irma damaged or destroyed 95% of the structures on Barbuda, including its hospital, schools and both of its hotels;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barbudad_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-barbudad-151">[151]</a></sup> it completely flattened some residential blocks while submerging others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> The destruction rendered the island's sole airport and much of its infrastructure inoperative—including water and telecommunication services—which further hampered relief efforts. Preliminary assessments on Barbuda suggest property damage of at least $150 million. A total of three storm-related deaths have been reported on the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barbuda_death_toll_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barbuda_death_toll-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to the catastrophic impact on Barbuda's human residents, concern turned to the storm's effects on the island's wildlife. The island's only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endemic" title="Endemic">endemic</a> bird, the <a href="/wiki/Near-threatened_species" title="Near-threatened species">near-threatened</a> <a href="/wiki/Barbuda_warbler" title="Barbuda warbler">Barbuda warbler</a>, numbered less than 2,000 individuals prior to the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birdscarib_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-birdscarib-154">[154]</a></sup> It is unknown if the warbler survived the hurricane or its aftermath.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birdscarib_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-birdscarib-154">[154]</a></sup> Barbuda's <a href="/wiki/Codrington_Lagoon" title="Codrington Lagoon">Codrington Lagoon</a>, home to the largest colony of <a href="/wiki/Magnificent_frigatebird" title="Magnificent frigatebird">magnificent frigatebirds</a> in the Caribbean, with an estimated 2,500 nesting pairs, was also inundated by the storm surge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birdscarib_154-2"><a href="#cite_note-birdscarib-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>Remaining just outside of Irma's strongest windfield, <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a> sustained minimal damage in the form of leveled roofs and fences, downed power poles and lines, and uprooted trees. Some street flooding also took place in low-lying areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Three people were treated for minor storm-related injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Disaster_risk_reduction" title="Disaster risk reduction">Forensic disaster analysts</a> from the Center for Disaster Management and Risk Reduction Technology (CEDIM), a Germany-based <a href="/wiki/Risk_management" title="Risk management">risk management</a> agency, estimate that economic losses for Antigua and Barbuda will exceed $120 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEDIM_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-CEDIM-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saint_Martin">Saint Martin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Saint Martin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Irma_on_Sint_Maarten_(NL)_05.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="833" data-file-width="1250" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Hurricane_Irma_on_Sint_Maarten_%28NL%29_05.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Irma_on_Sint_Maarten_%28NL%29_05.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Hurricane_Irma_on_Sint_Maarten_%28NL%29_05.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Irma_on_Sint_Maarten_%28NL%29_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Hurricane_Irma_on_Sint_Maarten_%28NL%29_05.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Irma_on_Sint_Maarten_%28NL%29_05.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Irma_on_Sint_Maarten_(NL)_05.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damaged buildings in <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a> on September 7, 2017</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the morning of September 6, Irma's center crossed the island of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a> while the storm was near peak intensity, sweeping away entire structures, submerging roads and cars, and triggering an island-wide blackout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Irma's extreme winds ripped trees out of the ground and sent vehicles and debris from damaged structures scattered across the territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-express_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-express-158">[158]</a></sup> On the French side of <a href="/wiki/Collectivity_of_Saint_Martin" title="Collectivity of Saint Martin">Saint-Martin</a>, entire marinas around <a href="/wiki/Marigot,_Saint_Martin" title="Marigot, Saint Martin">Marigot</a> were left in ruins, littered with the stranded remnants of boats that had smashed into each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-express_158-1"><a href="#cite_note-express-158">[158]</a></sup> A hotel caught on fire, but dangerous conditions and impassable roads prevented firefighters from putting out the blaze. Another hotel lost nearly all of its ground floor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Media images depicted devastated room interiors with furniture hurled around after the winds had shattered their windows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-express_158-2"><a href="#cite_note-express-158">[158]</a></sup> Irma killed four people on the French side of the island and injured 50 others, one of whom was in critical condition. As many as 95% of the buildings there were damaged to some degree; 60% of those were totally uninhabitable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lacroix_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-lacroix-160">[160]</a></sup> Estimates from CEDIM indicate a minimum of $950 million worth of economic losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEDIM_133-2"><a href="#cite_note-CEDIM-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>A similar situation unfolded in <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>, Saint Martin's Dutch half, as intense winds ripped through buildings and lifted vehicles aloft "as if they were matches".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sintmaartendutch_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-sintmaartendutch-161">[161]</a></sup> The hurricane wreaked havoc on <a href="/wiki/Princess_Juliana_International_Airport" title="Princess Juliana International Airport">Princess Juliana International Airport</a>, with "huge chunks of the building [strewn] across the runway and a jet bridge snapped in half."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sintmaarten_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-sintmaarten-162">[162]</a></sup> It demolished or severely damaged about 70% of Sint Maarten's houses, forcing thousands of residents into public shelters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abclatest_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-abclatest-163">[163]</a></sup> There were two deaths and 23 injuries, 11 of which were serious, in the Dutch territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> Irma is considered the worst natural disaster to hit Sint Maarten; the extent of its damage far exceeded that of any previous hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sintmaartendutch_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-sintmaartendutch-161">[161]</a></sup> Prime Minister William Marlin estimates that at least €1 billion ($1.2 billion) will be necessary to restore the destruction,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dmgsintmaarten_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-dmgsintmaarten-165">[165]</a></sup> while disaster analysts from CEDIM predict losses will exceed $1.5 billion. By September 9, 2017, the death count rose to 4 with one death due to natural causes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Saint_Barthélemy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Saint_Barth.C3.A9lemy">Saint Barthélemy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Saint Barthélemy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Irma left widespread destruction and disastrous flooding along its path over the French island of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Saint Barthélemy">Saint Barthélemy</a>, southeast of Saint Martin. Describing the extent of the destruction, one local compared it to "a bomb that burned all vegetation," while another said that it were as if the hurricane had effectively "erased the island from the map".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barts_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-barts-167">[167]</a></sup> Violent seas swept away entire coastal establishments, with one hotel being stripped of all but its foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bartsfr_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-bartsfr-168">[168]</a></sup> Streets in the capital of <a href="/wiki/Gustavia,_Saint_Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Gustavia, Saint Barthélemy">Gustavia</a> were turned into rushing rivers, which carried away vehicles and pieces of furniture. The island's fire station was inundated with up to 6.4 ft (2.0 m) of flood waters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bartsfr_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-bartsfr-168">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnncarib_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnncarib-169">[169]</a></sup> With scores of homes and much of the infrastructure destroyed, the majority of the island's population was left stranded and without water, electricity or phone service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barts_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-barts-167">[167]</a></sup> The associated economic losses could exceed $480 million according to CEDIM's analysts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEDIM_133-3"><a href="#cite_note-CEDIM-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>Preliminary assessments from the French government indicate that Hurricane Irma caused a combined €1.2 billion ($1.44 billion) in insured losses across the French territories of Saint-Martin and Saint Barts. This total covered private property such as homes, vehicles and businesses (including lost revenue);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frenchtotal_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-frenchtotal-170">[170]</a></sup> the extent of the damage to infrastructural and public facilities remains undetermined. Nonetheless, this made Irma one of the costliest natural disasters to hit the French Republic in 35 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frenchtotal_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-frenchtotal-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
