NOAA aircraft flying through the eye of Hurricane Irma on September 5, 2017</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anguilla">Anguilla</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Anguilla">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The British Overseas Territory of <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a> had the eye of the storm pass over it on September 6. Many homes and schools were destroyed, and the island's only hospital was badly damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anguilla_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anguilla-171">[171]</a></sup> The devastation was particularly severe in <a href="/wiki/East_End,_Anguilla" title="East End, Anguilla">East End</a>, where the winds uprooted scores of trees and power poles and demolished a number of houses. In <a href="/wiki/The_Valley,_Anguilla" title="The Valley, Anguilla">The Valley</a>, the island's capital, the hurricane blew out the windows of government buildings. Rough seas inflicted heavy damage upon several bays and harbors, and a seaside restaurant was completely eradicated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reportcarib_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-reportcarib-172">[172]</a></sup> About 90% of roads were left impassable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lacroix_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-lacroix-160">[160]</a></sup> The island's air traffic control tower was damaged, exacerbating the already poor communication with the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> One death was reported on the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anguilla_171-1"><a href="#cite_note-Anguilla-171">[171]</a></sup> According to CEDIM, Anguilla's economy could suffer at least $190 million in losses from the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEDIM_133-4"><a href="#cite_note-CEDIM-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saint_Lucia">Saint Lucia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Saint Lucia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Large swells ahead of Irma washed ashore debris and sea life in <a href="/wiki/Castries" title="Castries">Castries</a>, Saint Lucia, blocking some roads. Seaside roads were inundated with water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Barbados">Barbados</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Barbados">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>One surfer was killed amid rough surf in <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> after hitting a reef and breaking his neck. Trees were also destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bt_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-bt-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Guadeloupe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The hurricane's effects, such as violent seas and rattling trees, were intense enough to be detected by seismographs in <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>. Several houses were damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Around 8,000 households and a water supply network on that island lost power during the storm, leaving several communes in the dark without running water. Overall damage was limited to external parts of houses and trees that were blown onto roads and three unmanned ships wrecked by rough seas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guadeloupe_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupe-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Saint Kitts and Nevis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a> endured similar conditions to other islands. Blustery rainstorms triggered scattered power outages and disabled the island's water system, but per the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross" title="International Red Cross">International Red Cross</a>, the islands were spared the level of destruction seen elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RedCross1_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-RedCross1-177">[177]</a></sup> Still, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Harris" title="Timothy Harris">Timothy Harris</a> stated that property and infrastructure had sustained "significant damage."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islands_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-islands-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Dutch territories of <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a> were also struck by the hurricane's winds, resulting in infrastructural damage, water shortages and telecommunication outages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reportcarib_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-reportcarib-172">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saba_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Saba-178">[178]</a></sup> Several houses were left uninhabitable. On Saba, the hurricane also defoliated trees and injured a few people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reportcarib_172-2"><a href="#cite_note-reportcarib-172">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saba_178-1"><a href="#cite_note-Saba-178">[178]</a></sup> CEDIM's analysts expect economic losses of $20–65 million for the two islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEDIM_133-5"><a href="#cite_note-CEDIM-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Virgin_Islands">British Virgin Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: British Virgin Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Irma_turns_Virgin_Islands_brown.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Hurricane_Irma_turns_Virgin_Islands_brown.jpg/400px-Hurricane_Irma_turns_Virgin_Islands_brown.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Hurricane_Irma_turns_Virgin_Islands_brown.jpg/600px-Hurricane_Irma_turns_Virgin_Islands_brown.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ef/Hurricane_Irma_turns_Virgin_Islands_brown.jpg 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Irma_turns_Virgin_Islands_brown.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MODIS" title="MODIS">MODIS</a> imagery by <i><a href="/wiki/Aqua_(satellite)" title="Aqua (satellite)">Aqua</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Terra_(satellite)" title="Terra (satellite)">Terra</a></i> of the Virgin Islands from before Hurricane Irma's impact on August 25, 2017, and after on September 10, 2017, depicting a "browning" of the landscape and vegetation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_before_and_after_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_before_and_after-179">[179]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Damage in the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a> was extensive. Numerous buildings and roads were destroyed on the island of <a href="/wiki/Tortola" title="Tortola">Tortola</a>, which bore the brunt of the hurricane's core.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Along Cane Garden Bay, the storm surge submerged several seaside bars and a gas station. Satellite images revealed many of the island's residential zones had been left in ruins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reportcarib_172-3"><a href="#cite_note-reportcarib-172">[172]</a></sup> The hurricane passed over <a href="/wiki/Necker_Island_(British_Virgin_Islands)" title="Necker Island (British Virgin Islands)">Necker Island</a>, also causing severe damage and destroying the mansion of <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bransontrump_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-bransontrump-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most homes and businesses were destroyed on the island of <a href="/wiki/Jost_Van_Dyke" title="Jost Van Dyke">Jost Van Dyke</a>, the smallest of the B.V.I.'s four main islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes16_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes16-182">[182]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="Governor of the Virgin Islands">Governor</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gus_Jaspert" title="Gus Jaspert">Gus Jaspert</a>, who had only been sworn into office 13 days previously, declared a state of emergency - the first time this has ever happened in the Territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> After the storm authorities estimated that it would take 6 months to restore public electricity to the entire country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._Virgin_Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: U.S. Virgin Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:U.S._Navy_conducts_damage_assessments_in_the_U.S._Virgin_Islands.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
U.S. Navy video of damage assessments in the U.S. Virgin Islands</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Irma's effects in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="U.S. Virgin Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</a> were most profound on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Thomas</a>, where at least 12 inches (305 mm) of rain fell, and on <a href="/wiki/Saint_John,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint John, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint John</a>. Saint Thomas island suffered widespread structural damage, including to its police station and airport. Patients from the fourth and third floors of <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Amalie,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Charlotte Amalie, U.S. Virgin Islands">Charlotte Amalie</a>'s hospital had to be relocated to lower floors due to flooding from roof leaks. Three deaths were attributed to Irma on the island. On nearby <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a>, there were communication issues and some damage to the infrastructure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reportcarib_172-4"><a href="#cite_note-reportcarib-172">[172]</a></sup> Saint John lost access to ferry and cargo services, along with access to the local airport. Due to its normal reliance on electricity from Saint Thomas, the island was left without power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Puerto_Rico">Puerto Rico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Puerto Rico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Waves in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> reached 30 feet (9.1 m) in height;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islands_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-islands-55">[55]</a></sup> a 111 miles (179 km) per hour gust was measured on <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">Culebra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> Two people died due to rainstorms ahead of the hurricane: one man died in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orocovis" title="Orocovis">Orocovis</a> after falling off his ladder while repairing his roof; another man on the coast in <a href="/wiki/Capitanejo_(Ponce)" title="Capitanejo (Ponce)">Capitanejo</a> died after being struck by lightning. Three nearby fishermen were burned by the same lightning strike, but survived. Two other people died during the hurricane: a woman died while being evacuated from her house in a wheelchair and fell from the same hitting her head; another person died in a car accident in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Can%C3%B3vanas" title="Canóvanas">Canóvanas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puerto_Rico_deaths_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Puerto_Rico_deaths-190">[190]</a></sup> In rural <a href="/wiki/Lo%C3%ADza,_Puerto_Rico" title="Loíza, Puerto Rico">Loíza</a>, 79 homes were destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRgrid_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-PRgrid-191">[191]</a></sup> More than a million residents lost power due to damages caused by the storm, according to former Puerto Rican Governor <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Garc%C3%ADa_Padilla" title="Alejandro García Padilla">Alejandro García Padilla</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Governor <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Rossell%C3%B3" title="Ricardo Rosselló">Ricardo Rosselló</a> declared the islands of <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">Culebra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Vieques, Puerto Rico">Vieques</a> to be disaster areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islands_55-3"><a href="#cite_note-islands-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Hispaniola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:People_stand_in_a_flooded_street_that_usually_serves_as_a_farmers_market,_in_Ouanaminthe,_northeast_Haiti,_Sept._8,_2017._(Photo_-_Josiah_Cherenfant,_courtesy_VOA_Creole_Service).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="767" data-file-width="1023" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/People_stand_in_a_flooded_street_that_usually_serves_as_a_farmers_market%2C_in_Ouanaminthe%2C_northeast_Haiti%2C_Sept._8%2C_2017._%28Photo_-_Josiah_Cherenfant%2C_courtesy_VOA_Creole_Service%29.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/People_stand_in_a_flooded_street_that_usually_serves_as_a_farmers_market%2C_in_Ouanaminthe%2C_northeast_Haiti%2C_Sept._8%2C_2017._%28Photo_-_Josiah_Cherenfant%2C_courtesy_VOA_Creole_Service%29.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/People_stand_in_a_flooded_street_that_usually_serves_as_a_farmers_market%2C_in_Ouanaminthe%2C_northeast_Haiti%2C_Sept._8%2C_2017._%28Photo_-_Josiah_Cherenfant%2C_courtesy_VOA_Creole_Service%29.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:People_stand_in_a_flooded_street_that_usually_serves_as_a_farmers_market,_in_Ouanaminthe,_northeast_Haiti,_Sept._8,_2017._(Photo_-_Josiah_Cherenfant,_courtesy_VOA_Creole_Service).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
People stand in a flooded street that usually serves as a farmers market, in <a href="/wiki/Ouanaminthe" title="Ouanaminthe">Ouanaminthe</a>, northeast <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, September 8, 2017.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although spared a direct hit, both the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> were affected by high winds and heavy rains. A bridge over the <a href="/wiki/Dajab%C3%B3n_River" title="Dajabón River">Dajabón River</a> connecting the two countries was broken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxfam_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-oxfam-193">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the Dominican Republic, the fishing community of <a href="/wiki/Nagua" title="Nagua">Nagua</a> sustained damage from waves that destroyed homes. 55,000 soldiers were deployed to affected areas to help with the clean-up efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JamObsHelp_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-JamObsHelp-53">[53]</a></sup> By the evening of September 7, the government had counted 2,721 damaged homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOLA_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-NOLA-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Haiti, flooding one meter deep sat in residential neighborhoods in places like <a href="/wiki/Cap-Ha%C3%AFtien" title="Cap-Haïtien">Cap-Haïtien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ouanaminthe" title="Ouanaminthe">Ouanaminthe</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gonaives" title="Gonaives">Gonaives</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxfam_193-1"><a href="#cite_note-oxfam-193">[193]</a></sup> Mudslides, destroyed homes, flooded crops, and infrastructure damage were reported in the northern part of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOLA_54-3"><a href="#cite_note-NOLA-54">[54]</a></sup> The total expanse of the flooding stretched from <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B4le-Saint-Nicolas" title="Môle-Saint-Nicolas">Môle-Saint-Nicolas</a> in the west to the eastern border with the Dominican Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HaitiFarms_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-HaitiFarms-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turks_and_Caicos_Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Turks and Caicos Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On the evening of September 7, at 7:30 pm AST (<small>23:30 UTC</small>), Hurricane Irma reached the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>. While the eye passed just south of the main islands, crossing over <a href="/wiki/South_Caicos" title="South Caicos">South Caicos</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ambergris_Cay" title="Ambergris Cay">Ambergris Cays</a>, the most powerful winds on the northern side of the eye swept all of the islands for more than two hours. Communications infrastructure was destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SouthCaicos_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-SouthCaicos-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 8, Minister of Infrastructure Goldray Ewing confirmed that damage to <a href="/wiki/Providenciales" title="Providenciales">Providenciales</a> was extensive, with the northwestern neighborhood of Blue Hill being "gone." He estimated that damage on Providenciales alone would total US$500 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> The hospital in the capital, <a href="/wiki/Cockburn_Town" title="Cockburn Town">Cockburn Town</a>, was damaged, but no deaths or injuries have been reported as of yet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> On South Caicos, 75% of roofs were lost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SouthCaicos_197-1"><a href="#cite_note-SouthCaicos-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bahamas">The Bahamas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: The Bahamas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a>, the eye of the storm passed over Duncan Town, the major settlement of the <a href="/wiki/Ragged_Island,_Bahamas" title="Ragged Island, Bahamas">Ragged Islands chain</a>, on September 8. It also passed "almost directly over" <a href="/wiki/Inagua" title="Inagua">Inagua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acklins" title="Acklins">South Acklins</a>, according to the Bahamas Department of Meteorology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup></p>
<p>Damages were largely confined to the southern islands starting the morning of September 8. On <a href="/wiki/Mayaguana" title="Mayaguana">Mayaguana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inagua" title="Inagua">Great Inagua</a>, downed power lines knocked out communications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> On Great Inagua, 70% of homes sustained roof damage, and the island's school lost its roof entirely. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morton_Salt_Company" title="Morton Salt Company">Morton Salt Company</a>'s signature production facility, one of the major employers in the country, experienced millions of dollars in damages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The Acklins settlement of Salina Point was cut off from the rest of the island by flooding, while <a href="/wiki/Crooked_Island,_Bahamas" title="Crooked Island, Bahamas">Crooked Island</a> had widespread roof damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT9_62-3"><a href="#cite_note-NYT9-62">[62]</a></sup> In the northern Bahamas, the worst property damage came on September 10 as the outer bands of the system produced <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadic activity</a> on <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bahama" title="Grand Bahama">Grand Bahama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bimini" title="Bimini">Bimini</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BStornadoes_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-BStornadoes-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Patrol_301,_Admiral_Didiez_Burgos_of_the_Dominican_Navy_delivering_disaster_supplies_in_Havana_Harbor_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg"><img alt="The Patrol 301, Admiral Didiez Burgos of the Dominican Navy delivering disaster supplies in Havana Harbor after Hurricane Irma." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1348" data-file-width="2392" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/The_Patrol_301%2C_Admiral_Didiez_Burgos_of_the_Dominican_Navy_delivering_disaster_supplies_in_Havana_Harbor_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/220px-The_Patrol_301%2C_Admiral_Didiez_Burgos_of_the_Dominican_Navy_delivering_disaster_supplies_in_Havana_Harbor_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/The_Patrol_301%2C_Admiral_Didiez_Burgos_of_the_Dominican_Navy_delivering_disaster_supplies_in_Havana_Harbor_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/330px-The_Patrol_301%2C_Admiral_Didiez_Burgos_of_the_Dominican_Navy_delivering_disaster_supplies_in_Havana_Harbor_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/The_Patrol_301%2C_Admiral_Didiez_Burgos_of_the_Dominican_Navy_delivering_disaster_supplies_in_Havana_Harbor_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/440px-The_Patrol_301%2C_Admiral_Didiez_Burgos_of_the_Dominican_Navy_delivering_disaster_supplies_in_Havana_Harbor_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Patrol_301,_Admiral_Didiez_Burgos_of_the_Dominican_Navy_delivering_disaster_supplies_in_Havana_Harbor_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Patrol 301, Admiral Didiez Burgos of the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Navy" title="Dominican Navy">Dominican Navy</a> delivering disaster supplies in <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> Harbor after Hurricane Irma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Late on September 8, Irma reintensified into a Category 5 hurricane and made landfall on the <a href="/wiki/Sabana-Camag%C3%BCey_Archipelago" title="Sabana-Camagüey Archipelago">Camagüey Archipelago</a> off the northern coast of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, with maximum sustained winds of 160 mph (260 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup></p>
<p>The weather station at <a href="/wiki/Esmeralda,_Cuba" title="Esmeralda, Cuba">Esmeralda, Camagüey</a> was damaged, with the wind gauge destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian8_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-guardian8-101">[101]</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, northern Cuba experienced "waves more than 16 feet high, and damage to hospitals, factories and warehouses."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT9_62-4"><a href="#cite_note-NYT9-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>By late morning on September 9, Irma had weakened to Category 3 due to the Cuban topography but continued to cause significant damage. The tourist areas of <a href="/wiki/Cayo_Coco" title="Cayo Coco">Cayo Coco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cayo_Guillermo" title="Cayo Guillermo">Cayo Guillermo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cayo_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa" title="Cayo Santa María">Cayo Santa María</a> and the nearby town of <a href="/wiki/Caibari%C3%A9n" title="Caibarién">Caibarién</a> received the brunt of the storm, with waves rolling through town and the characteristic one-story homes completely flooded. Flooding worsened as the hurricane moved west, pushing the <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a> along to the regions around <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> By the afternoon, limited flooding was occurring in Havana, including around the <a href="/wiki/Malec%C3%B3n,_Havana" title="Malecón, Havana">Malecón</a>. Widespread destruction of housing was reported in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Ciego_de_%C3%81vila_Province" title="Ciego de Ávila Province">Ciego de Ávila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Villa_Clara_Province" title="Villa Clara Province">Villa Clara</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT9_62-5"><a href="#cite_note-NYT9-62">[62]</a></sup> In the city of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara,_Cuba" title="Santa Clara, Cuba">Santa Clara</a>, 39 buildings collapsed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zombies_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-zombies-215">[215]</a></sup> Overall, Irma is estimated to have caused at least $2.2 billion (2017 USD) in damage and at least 10 deaths across the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fx112-ch-article_138-2"><a href="#cite_note-fx112-ch-article-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cubadeaths_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cubadeaths-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hurricane Irma directly impacted a major colony of <a href="/wiki/American_flamingo" title="American flamingo">American flamingos</a> on Cuba's northern <a href="/wiki/Cayo_Coco" title="Cayo Coco">Cayo Coco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birdscarib_154-3"><a href="#cite_note-birdscarib-154">[154]</a></sup> Early reports from <i>Diario de Cuba</i> indicated that several hundred flamingos had been killed by the storm, though other estimates ranged as high as several thousand birds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birdscarib_154-4"><a href="#cite_note-birdscarib-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainland_United_States_2">Mainland United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Mainland United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sedimentation_around_South_Florida_and_Bahamas_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="673" data-file-width="1199" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sedimentation_around_South_Florida_and_Bahamas_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/220px-Sedimentation_around_South_Florida_and_Bahamas_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sedimentation_around_South_Florida_and_Bahamas_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/330px-Sedimentation_around_South_Florida_and_Bahamas_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sedimentation_around_South_Florida_and_Bahamas_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/440px-Sedimentation_around_South_Florida_and_Bahamas_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sedimentation_around_South_Florida_and_Bahamas_after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
True-color images before and after the passage of Irma, in which light blue indicates sediment suspended in the water, kicked up by the intensity of the storm<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Preliminary estimates place the amount of damage what Hurricane Irma caused in the US at a minimum of $50 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assess_damage_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-assess_damage-146">[146]</a></sup> Hurricane Irma affected multiple states in the South, notably Florida. Except for the Florida Keys, the total damage it caused was not as great as government officials and forecasters had warned. The Florida Keys suffered the worst of the damage in the US. After surveying the aftermath of Irma, Florida governor Rick Scott said "I thought we would see more damage" [on the mainland] but said "he witnessed devastation in the Keys".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> Hurricane Irma weakened after making landfall in Cuba, but strengthened back into a Category 4 prior to hitting the Keys. President Donald Trump commented on Twitter that the devastation in some places was "far greater than anyone thought".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup></p>
<p>At least 88 people died throughout the United States in relation to Hurricane Irma: 80 in Florida, 5 in South Carolina, and 3 in Georgia.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida_2">Florida</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Florida">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miami_Beach_-_Hurricane_Irma_2017_14.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5152" data-file-width="7668" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Miami_Beach_-_Hurricane_Irma_2017_14.jpg/220px-Miami_Beach_-_Hurricane_Irma_2017_14.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Miami_Beach_-_Hurricane_Irma_2017_14.jpg/330px-Miami_Beach_-_Hurricane_Irma_2017_14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Miami_Beach_-_Hurricane_Irma_2017_14.jpg/440px-Miami_Beach_-_Hurricane_Irma_2017_14.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miami_Beach_-_Hurricane_Irma_2017_14.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Light pole with lamp torn away and landing about 50 feet away. Corner of Washington Avenue and Lincoln Lane, Miami Beach</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Throughout Florida, at least 80 people died in storm-related incidents. The majority of deaths occurred from drowning, trauma, and carbon monoxide poisoning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72Deaths_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-72Deaths-220">[220]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NursingHome12_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-NursingHome12-221">[221]</a></sup> At least 12 people died throughout the Florida Keys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MH_0923deaths_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-MH_0923deaths-222">[222]</a></sup> One death occurred during preparations when a man fell off a ladder, while installing hurricane shutters in <a href="/wiki/Davie,_Florida" title="Davie, Florida">Davie</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davie_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-davie-223">[223]</a></sup> Another death occurred in a traffic accident in tropical storm force winds in <a href="/wiki/Monroe_County,_Florida" title="Monroe County, Florida">Monroe County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> A man in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coconut_Grove,_Florida" title="Coconut Grove, Florida">Coconut Grove</a> died while riding out the storm on his houseboat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> Three deaths occurred in <a href="/wiki/Polk_County,_Florida" title="Polk County, Florida">Polk County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> In the hurricane's aftermath, lack of power and possible criminal negligence led to 12 deaths at a nursing home in <a href="/wiki/Hollywood,_Florida" title="Hollywood, Florida">Hollywood</a>. The patients died from sweltering heat worsened by the lack of air conditioning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NursingHome12_221-1"><a href="#cite_note-NursingHome12-221">[221]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Irma_and_Jose_(36429922693).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="798" data-file-width="1200" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Hurricane_Irma_and_Jose_%2836429922693%29.jpg/260px-Hurricane_Irma_and_Jose_%2836429922693%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Hurricane_Irma_and_Jose_%2836429922693%29.jpg/390px-Hurricane_Irma_and_Jose_%2836429922693%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Hurricane_Irma_and_Jose_%2836429922693%29.jpg/520px-Hurricane_Irma_and_Jose_%2836429922693%29.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Irma_and_Jose_(36429922693).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hurricane Irma on September 10, right before landfall on Florida. <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Hurricane Jose</a> can be seen to the lower right.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After crossing the <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Florida" title="Straits of Florida">Straits of Florida</a> and being upgraded to a Category 4 hurricane, initial landfall took place at <a href="/wiki/Cudjoe_Key,_Florida" title="Cudjoe Key, Florida">Cudjoe Key</a> at 9:10 am. EDT on September 10,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> where an estimated 10 ft (3 m) storm surge occurred during the afternoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> In the Keys, the hurricane caused major damage to buildings, <a href="/wiki/Trailer_park" title="Trailer park">trailer parks</a>, boats, roads, the electricity supply, mobile phone coverage, internet access, sanitation, the water supply and the fuel supply. Key West, <a href="/wiki/Sugarloaf_Key" title="Sugarloaf Key">Sugarloaf Key</a>, <a href="/wiki/Summerland_Key" title="Summerland Key">Summerland Key</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ramrod_Key" title="Ramrod Key">Ramrod Key</a>, <a href="/wiki/Little_Torch_Key" title="Little Torch Key">Little Torch Key</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_Pine_Key,_Florida" title="Big Pine Key, Florida">Big Pine Key</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marathon,_Florida" title="Marathon, Florida">Marathon</a> were also flooded by storm surge,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadoes</a> were reported at Sugarloaf Key.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup></p>
<p>A second landfall was made, as a Category 3 hurricane, at <a href="/wiki/Marco_Island,_Florida" title="Marco Island, Florida">Marco Island</a> at 3:35 pm. EDT the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> A 7 ft (2.1 m) storm surge occurred in <a href="/wiki/Naples,_Florida" title="Naples, Florida">Naples</a>, which Irma passed over as a Category 2 hurricane after being downgraded at 5 pm. EDT.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> Part of <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay" title="Tampa Bay">Tampa Bay</a> (at Hillsborough Bay) was drained in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reverse_storm_surge" title="Reverse storm surge">reverse storm surge</a> caused by the storm's pressure differential, prior to the arrival of the eye of the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sarasota_Bay" title="Sarasota Bay">Sarasota Bay</a> was also drained, resulting in the stranding of two <a href="/wiki/Manatee" title="Manatee">manatees</a> which were then rescued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> The hurricane was downgraded to Category 1, prior to reaching <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup></p>
<p>Away from the path of the eye, a wind gust of 109 mph (175 km/h) was recorded in <a href="/wiki/Pembroke_Pines,_Florida" title="Pembroke Pines, Florida">Pembroke Pines</a>. In Miami, storm surge inundated <a href="/wiki/Brickell_Avenue" title="Brickell Avenue">Brickell Avenue</a> with waist-deep water,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PP_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-PP-244">[244]</a></sup> and two high-rise <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tower_crane" title="Tower crane">tower cranes</a> collapsed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> A further construction crane collapsed in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale,_Florida" title="Fort Lauderdale, Florida">Fort Lauderdale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> There were sporadic reports of <a href="/wiki/Looting" title="Looting">looting</a> and burglaries at several <a href="/wiki/Miami_metropolitan_area" title="Miami metropolitan area">Miami Metro area</a> businesses with the theft of non-essential items such as <a href="/wiki/Sportswear_(activewear)" title="Sportswear (activewear)">sports apparel</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletic_shoes" title="Athletic shoes">athletic shoes</a> during the height of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a>, flooding surpassed the record set by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dora" title="Hurricane Dora">Hurricane Dora</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Overflight_of_Jacksonville,_Florida,_after_Hurricane_Irma.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Overflight of Jacksonville, Florida, after Hurricane Irma</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At 1:00 pm. EDT, on September 10, almost 730,000 customers were without power in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County" title="Miami-Dade County">Miami-Dade County</a> alone, with almost 500,000 without power in Broward County, over 225,000 out in Palm Beach County, and in total approximately 1,572,000 customers were without power across the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> As of 6:41 pm. EDT on September 10 over 2.6 million homes in Florida were without power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> Air traffic was reduced; at one point on September 10, there were no airliners over Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the days after the hurricane, due to the heavy rainfall, numerous rivers had flooded their surrounding land, including residential areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> Public health risks, such as diarrheal infections and mosquito-borne illnesses, remain from the flooding that resulted in the aftermath of the hurricane. A large concern from flooding is contamination because people become exposed to dirty floodwaters and the potential for contaminated water to get into the local water supply is significant. One example of an illness that can get into the water supply is <a href="/wiki/Leptospirosis" title="Leptospirosis">leptospirosis</a>, which is caused by rat urine being in the floodwaters. If people are exposed to leptospirosis and do not get treatment, it can cause kidney damage, <a href="/wiki/Meningitis" title="Meningitis">meningitis</a>, and liver failure. <a href="/wiki/Norovirus" title="Norovirus">Noroviruses</a> and other infections are also a risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_states">Other states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Other states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Three deaths were reported in <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> due to falling trees and debris, along with widespread wind damage and power outages throughout the state primarily due to fallen trees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABC49763467_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABC49763467-255">[255]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Tybee_Island,_Georgia" title="Tybee Island, Georgia">Tybee Island</a>, the storm surge caused extensive flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston, South Carolina</a>, the third highest storm surge on record was recorded, reaching a height of approximately 10 ft (3 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> By of September 12, almost 100,000 had lost power in <a href="/wiki/Upstate_South_Carolina" title="Upstate South Carolina">Upstate</a> South Carolina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup> Five people died in storm-related incidents across South Carolina, all from indirect incidents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5scdeaths_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-5scdeaths-259">[259]</a></sup></p>
<p>Light damage occurred in other areas, including <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> About 75,000 customers in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> lost power due to Irma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the immediate aftermath of Hurricane Irma's path through the West Indies and Caribbean, the devastation to roads, harbors and airports significantly impeded the transportation and distribution of relief supplies. Foreign countries moved to provide much of the initial aid. The British, Dutch, French, and United States governments sent warships and planes with supplies and manpower to the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JamObsHelp_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-JamObsHelp-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USSmil_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-USSmil-262">[262]</a></sup> International leaders, including Dutch King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Willem-Alexander" title="Willem-Alexander">Willem-Alexander</a> and French President <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Macron" title="Emmanuel Macron">Emmanuel Macron</a>, quickly moved to visit affected territories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-willem_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-willem-263">[263]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-macron_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-macron-264">[264]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some of the affected countries and territories also offered assistance to each other. Cuba, which sustained extensive damage from the storm, sent 750 health workers to Antigua and Barbuda, Saint Kitts and Nevis, Saint Lucia, The Bahamas, Dominica, and Haiti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cubadocs_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-cubadocs-265">[265]</a></sup> Government officials and members of the public in Puerto Rico delivered assistance and evacuated people stranded on other islands. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Citizenship_and_Immigration_Services" title="U.S. Citizenship and Immigration Services">U.S. Citizenship and Immigration Services</a> granted special 30-day humanitarian visas for British Virgin Islanders to stay in Puerto Rico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRhelps_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-PRhelps-266">[266]</a></sup> Hundreds of people stranded on Saint Martin were flown to the Dominican Republic on humanitarian grounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antigua_and_Barbuda_2">Antigua and Barbuda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Antigua and Barbuda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In response to Hurricane Jose's approach, the Government of Antigua and Barbuda issued a mandatory evacuation on September 9 for any remaining residents on Barbuda. A Miami cargo plane landed on Antigua later that day, carrying over 60 tons (120,000 lbs) of relief supplies for the displaced storm victims—including bottled water, canned food and power generators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Overseas_Territories">British Overseas Territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: British Overseas Territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UK_Royal_Logistics_Corps_Mexflote_arrives_in_Anguilla.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="351" data-file-width="624" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/UK_Royal_Logistics_Corps_Mexflote_arrives_in_Anguilla.jpg/220px-UK_Royal_Logistics_Corps_Mexflote_arrives_in_Anguilla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/UK_Royal_Logistics_Corps_Mexflote_arrives_in_Anguilla.jpg/330px-UK_Royal_Logistics_Corps_Mexflote_arrives_in_Anguilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/UK_Royal_Logistics_Corps_Mexflote_arrives_in_Anguilla.jpg/440px-UK_Royal_Logistics_Corps_Mexflote_arrives_in_Anguilla.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

A UK Royal Logistics Corp landing raft delivers emergency relief to Anguilla</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Priti_Patel_in_the_Hurricane_Irma_Crisis_Operations_Room_(37124490675).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2667" data-file-width="4000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Priti_Patel_in_the_Hurricane_Irma_Crisis_Operations_Room_%2837124490675%29.jpg/220px-Priti_Patel_in_the_Hurricane_Irma_Crisis_Operations_Room_%2837124490675%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Priti_Patel_in_the_Hurricane_Irma_Crisis_Operations_Room_%2837124490675%29.jpg/330px-Priti_Patel_in_the_Hurricane_Irma_Crisis_Operations_Room_%2837124490675%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Priti_Patel_in_the_Hurricane_Irma_Crisis_Operations_Room_%2837124490675%29.jpg/440px-Priti_Patel_in_the_Hurricane_Irma_Crisis_Operations_Room_%2837124490675%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Priti_Patel_in_the_Hurricane_Irma_Crisis_Operations_Room_(37124490675).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
British <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_International_Development" title="Secretary of State for International Development">Secretary of State for International Development</a> <a href="/wiki/Priti_Patel" title="Priti Patel">Priti Patel</a> being briefed by her staff on the hurricane</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/RFA_Mounts_Bay_(L3008)" title="RFA Mounts Bay (L3008)">RFA <i>Mounts Bay</i></a> stationed itself near Anguilla and provided support and relief work to the island with its helicopters and 40 marines and army engineers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anguilla_171-2"><a href="#cite_note-Anguilla-171">[171]</a></sup> The ship delivered 6 tonnes of emergency aid to Anguilla and army engineers repaired a fuel leak at Anguilla's main petrol dump, restored power to the island's hospital and provided shelters for those left homeless by the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFA_Mounts_Bay_in_BVI_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-RFA_Mounts_Bay_in_BVI-269">[269]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_continues_to_deliver_vital_aid_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK_continues_to_deliver_vital_aid-270">[270]</a></sup> The ship arrived in the British Virgin Islands on September 8, 2017 to provide emergency relief to the islands, including providing shelters, food and water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFA_Mounts_Bay_in_BVI_269-1"><a href="#cite_note-RFA_Mounts_Bay_in_BVI-269">[269]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ocean_(L12)" title="HMS Ocean (L12)">HMS <i>Ocean</i></a> was diverted from the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> to provide relief from <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> to the affected British Overseas Territories of Anguilla, British Virgin Islands and Turks and Caicos on September 7, 2017,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> and aid is also being supplied by the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Development" title="Department for International Development">Department for International Development</a> from their disaster response centre at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kemble_Airfield" title="Kemble Airfield">Kemble Airfield</a>. As part of a £32 million operation named Operation Ruman, nearly 500 UK military personnel with emergency relief were dispatched from <a href="/wiki/RAF_Brize_Norton" title="RAF Brize Norton">RAF Brize Norton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> The British government also drafted 2 members of the UK police calibre into the region on September 10, 2017 and 53 police officers are to be drafted from RAF Brize Norton to the affected British Overseas Territories on September 15, 2017 to help maintain order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> UK politicians, including the chairs of the foreign affairs and development select committees, criticized both the government's preparations for the storm and its response as inadequate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMviolence_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-SMviolence-275">[275]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup></p>

</div>
</div>
<p>By September 12, 2017, the Department for International Development had delivered more than 40 tonnes of aid into the region, including into Turks and Caicos, and 1,000 UK military troops were deployed in the region as part of relief efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_continues_to_deliver_vital_aid_270-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK_continues_to_deliver_vital_aid-270">[270]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>, pledged an additional £25 million worth of funding as part of relief efforts in the region on September 13, 2017 and the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Affairs" title="Secretary of State for Foreign and Commonwealth Affairs">Secretary of State for Foreign and Commonwealth Affairs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a>, said that a further 250 UK military personnel would be deployed into the area within the next few days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnson_sees_impact_277-0"><a href="#cite_note-Johnson_sees_impact-277">[277]</a></sup> Anguilla's Chief Minister, <a href="/wiki/Victor_Banks" title="Victor Banks">Victor Banks</a>, praised the British government's response to the storm and said that Boris Johnson's visit to the island "sends a very positive signal to Anguillans that the British are serious about their response to this very severe hurricane", but went on to say that the current financial commitment from the UK was not substantial enough.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnson_sees_impact_277-1"><a href="#cite_note-Johnson_sees_impact-277">[277]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup></p>
<p>By September 15, 2017, the United Kingdom had over 70 military personnel and 4 police officers in Anguilla and had delivered 15 tonnes of aid to the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_response_in_numbers_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK_response_in_numbers-279">[279]</a></sup> In the British Virgin Islands, Royal Marines had cleared the airfield so that it was operational for the delivery of aid into the islands, with more than 200 British military personnel and 54 UK police officers on the ground and 8 tonnes of aid delivered to the islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_response_in_numbers_279-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK_response_in_numbers-279">[279]</a></sup> 120 British military personnel were on the ground in Turks and Caicos and over 150 shelter kits and 720 litres of water were delivered to the islands on September 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_response_in_numbers_279-2"><a href="#cite_note-UK_response_in_numbers-279">[279]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bahamas_2">The Bahamas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: The Bahamas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>By the afternoon of September 9, Bahamas Power and Light Company had dispatched crews across the archipelago to repair infrastructure damage. The southernmost islands, which were most severely affected by Irma's eye, remained largely inaccessible for days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup> Assessments showed that 15% of the national telecommunications network had been affected, with at least one tower destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bahamasair" title="Bahamasair">Bahamasair</a> resumed a limited domestic schedule on September 10, with international flights still cancelled due to existing and anticipated destruction at other destinations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup></p>
<p>The worst devastation occurred on <a href="/wiki/Ragged_Island,_Bahamas" title="Ragged Island, Bahamas">Ragged Island</a>, over which Irma's eye had directly passed. After days of the National Emergency Management Agency not being able to physically reach the island, officials were finally able to inspect it; they promptly declared it uninhabitable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RaggedUnlivable_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-RaggedUnlivable-283">[283]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup> Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Minnis" title="Hubert Minnis">Hubert Minnis</a> said that it was the worst disaster area he or his officials had ever seen, and that all remaining residents would need to leave, potentially permanently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RaggedUnlivable_283-1"><a href="#cite_note-RaggedUnlivable-283">[283]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup> Business leaders and other officials called for a new long-term development model to shift the population away from such sparsely-settled islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup></p>
<p>On <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bahama" title="Grand Bahama">Grand Bahama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bimini" title="Bimini">Bimini</a>, where tornadoes associated with Irma touched down on September 10, more than 100 people were left displaced. Infrastructure damage included docks, parks, and the power system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BStornadoes_204-1"><a href="#cite_note-BStornadoes-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aside from tangible asset losses, Irma brought significant economic damages. International freight shipping was projected to be offline for a week, and costs for rebuilding supplies were inflated due to demand in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba_2">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Swollen rivers contributed to worsening flooding in the days after the storm system left, resulting in additional evacuations. Officials resorted to using inflatable rafts to access affected areas. The national electrical infrastructure was said to be extensively damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zombies_215-1"><a href="#cite_note-zombies-215">[215]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hispaniola_2">Hispaniola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Hispaniola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the Dominican Republic, flooding worsened following Irma's departure, leading the number of displaced persons to increase to more than 24,000 by September 8. President <a href="/wiki/Danilo_Medina" title="Danilo Medina">Danilo Medina</a> ordered further evacuations due to at-risk dams, while the government banned swimming in rivers and ordered boats kept in port.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup> More than 422,000 people were left without water due to 28 aqueducts being damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Haiti, officials stated that losses were greater than they could have been since people largely did not heed early preparation and evacuation warnings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOLA_54-4"><a href="#cite_note-NOLA-54">[54]</a></sup> At least 5,000 homes were flooded. One man died trying to cross a flooded river; another went missing and 17 were injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup> The trash- and waste-contaminated floodwaters in places like <a href="/wiki/Cap-Ha%C3%AFtien" title="Cap-Haïtien">Cap-Haïtien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ouanaminthe" title="Ouanaminthe">Ouanaminthe</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gonaives" title="Gonaives">Gonaives</a> led to fears of <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> outbreaks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxfam_193-2"><a href="#cite_note-oxfam-193">[193]</a></sup> Flooding continued to worsen days after the storm, as runoff from the mountains swelled rivers in low-lying farming communities. United Nations peacekeepers from <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> were able to gain access to the flooded northwest region to provide urgent aid, but non-governmental organizations and Haitian economists warned that the estimated 30,000 victims would need longer-term assistance as well. Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jack_Guy_Lafontant" title="Jack Guy Lafontant">Jack Guy Lafontant</a> appointed a government commission to address Irma's effects, with <a href="/wiki/Action_Against_Hunger" title="Action Against Hunger">Action Against Hunger</a> in charge of humanitarian coordination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HaitiFarms_194-1"><a href="#cite_note-HaitiFarms-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Puerto_Rico_2">Puerto Rico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Puerto Rico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a></div>
<p>By September 9, more than one million Puerto Ricans were still without power, tens of thousands were without water, and several thousand were still in shelters. Hospitals were operating on generator power. The government was struggling to establish contact with the islands of <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">Culebra</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vieques" title="Vieques">Vieques</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islands_55-4"><a href="#cite_note-islands-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>By September 10, the main island had recovered enough to serve as a refuge for people stranded on other islands, including 1,200 tourists from Saint Martin and the U.S. Virgin Islands. Airlifts had brought more than 50 patients to Puerto Rico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRhelps_266-1"><a href="#cite_note-PRhelps-266">[266]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saint_Martin_2">Saint Martin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Saint Martin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Damage to Sint Maarten's harbour and to <a href="/wiki/Princess_Juliana_International_Airport" title="Princess Juliana International Airport">Princess Juliana International Airport</a> left the Dutch part of Saint Martin unreachable, although the smaller <a href="/wiki/Grand_Case-Esp%C3%A9rance_Airport" title="Grand Case-Espérance Airport">Grand Case-Espérance Airport</a> on the French side could be reopened by September 7 for supply aid by helicopter and airplane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup> The French armed forces based in <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Guyana" title="French Guyana">French Guyana</a> flew equipment and troops on board a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Casa_transport_aircraft&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Casa transport aircraft (page does not exist)">CASA/IPTN CN-235</a>.</p>
<p>The following day, the Dutch military was able to airlift <a href="/wiki/Dialysis" title="Dialysis">dialysis</a> patients off the island while also dropping leaflets to warn islanders about the rapidly approaching <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Hurricane Jose</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian8_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-guardian8-101">[101]</a></sup> Although the airport was closed, 435 students and faculty of the American University of the Caribbean were evacuated by the U.S. military.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> On September 10, Dutch King Willem-Alexander departed for the region, with intentions to visit Sint Maarten and other affected Dutch territories and commonwealth members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-willem_263-1"><a href="#cite_note-willem-263">[263]</a></sup></p>
<p>French President Emmanuel Macron followed this announcement by stating his intentions to visit the French part of the island on September 12 in order to bring aid supplies. In response to criticism of the French handling of the disaster, 1,000 troops, police, and other emergency workers were sent to Saint Martin and Saint Barthélemy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-macron_264-1"><a href="#cite_note-macron-264">[264]</a></sup></p>
<p>On both sides of Saint Martin, desperate conditions combined with food and water shortages in Irma's aftermath led to reports of violence, scavenging, and theft. In response, the French government increased its troop deployment to 2,200 and the Dutch government sent more than 600 military and police personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMviolence_275-1"><a href="#cite_note-SMviolence-275">[275]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_Overseas_Departments">French Overseas Departments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: French Overseas Departments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The day after the hurricane hit <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Barthelemy" title="Saint Barthelemy">Saint Barthelemy</a> the French armed forces based in <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Guyana" title="French Guyana">French Guyana</a> flew equipment and troops into the reopened <a href="/wiki/Airport" title="Airport">Grand Case-Espérance Airport</a>. On the September 7 and 9 equipment and personnel were flown from France to Guadeloupe and <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida_3">Florida</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Florida">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Florida_night-time_satellite_image_before-and-after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="1200" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Florida_night-time_satellite_image_before-and-after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/330px-Florida_night-time_satellite_image_before-and-after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Florida_night-time_satellite_image_before-and-after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/495px-Florida_night-time_satellite_image_before-and-after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Florida_night-time_satellite_image_before-and-after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg/660px-Florida_night-time_satellite_image_before-and-after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Florida_night-time_satellite_image_before-and-after_Hurricane_Irma.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Night-time satellite images of Florida before (<i>left</i>) and the night after (<i>right</i>) Hurricane Irma, highlighting the extensive loss of grid (mains) electricity</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On September 11, Florida Governor <a href="/wiki/Rick_Scott" title="Rick Scott">Rick Scott</a> conducted an aerial tour to survey the damage to the Keys. The <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Highway" title="Overseas Highway">Overseas Highway</a> remained closed while authorities assessed the integrity of the 42 bridges along the route.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup> Residents returning to the Keys were faced with a police roadblock, to the south of <a href="/wiki/Florida_City,_Florida" title="Florida City, Florida">Florida City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/USS_Iwo_Jima_(LHD-7)" title="USS Iwo Jima (LHD-7)">USS <i>Iwo Jima</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_New_York_(LPD-21)" title="USS New York (LPD-21)">USS <i>New York</i></a> and aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/USS_Abraham_Lincoln_(CVN-72)" title="USS Abraham Lincoln (CVN-72)">USS <i>Abraham Lincoln</i></a> were sent to the Keys area to aid with the recovery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the morning of September 12, some residents were allowed to return into the Keys as far as <a href="/wiki/Islamorada,_Florida" title="Islamorada, Florida">Islamorada</a>. Although road damage blocked entry any further than Islamorada, bridges had been inspected and found safe to <a href="/wiki/Sugarloaf_Key" title="Sugarloaf Key">Sugarloaf Key</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">FEMA</a>'s initial estimate indicated that 25% of buildings in the Keys were destroyed, 65% were significantly damaged, and 90% of houses sustained "some damage".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> By the evening, the Overseas Highway had been repaired and the bridges inspected as safe for <a href="/wiki/First_responder" title="First responder">first responders</a> to travel to Key West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup> On September 16, residents were free to return to Marathon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> Residents were allowed to return to Key West the following day, although the Keys remained closed to tourists and a checkpoint remained in place in Florida City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup></p>
<p>By September 12, almost 4.4 million homes and businesses in Florida were without power, according to state officials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_AFP_death_toll_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-World_AFP_death_toll-144">[144]</a></sup> Due mainly to the widespread loss of power, cell phone service was also significantly impacted after battery backup power for cell phone towers ran out and backup generators ran out of fuel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup> In an impact report by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">FCC</a>, as of 11 AM EDT on September 12, 89 of 108 (82%) cell phone towers were non-functioning in Monroe County (Florida Keys), 154 of 212 (73%) were non-functioning in Collier County (Naples), 36 of 46 (78%) were non-functioning in <a href="/wiki/Hendry_County,_Florida" title="Hendry County, Florida">Hendry County</a>, and an additional six counties had 41-60% of cell phone towers not functioning, including Lee County (Ft. Myers) and Miami-Dade County.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup></p>
<p>From September 12, <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">NOAA</a> released map-format aerial reconnaissance image data along the length of the Keys, and the coast around Naples and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Myers,_Florida" title="Fort Myers, Florida">Fort Myers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following Irma's passage, a 15 ft (4.6 m) hand-carved wooden canoe was discovered on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_River_(Florida)" title="Indian River (Florida)">Indian River</a> and could be several hundred years old. The state has removed the canoe for examination and safe keeping.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._Virgin_Islands_2">U.S. Virgin Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: U.S. Virgin Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the U.S. Virgin Islands, residents and tourists alike were described as being in a state of traumatic shock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zombies_215-2"><a href="#cite_note-zombies-215">[215]</a></sup> By September 7, the <a href="/wiki/USS_Wasp_(LHD-1)" title="USS Wasp (LHD-1)">USS <i>Wasp</i></a> amphibious assault ship had arrived in the U.S. Virgin Islands to provide supplies, damage assessment, and evacuation assistance. Four additional warships, some of which had already been on their way to Texas to assist with <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Hurricane Harvey</a> relief, were redirected to the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USSmil_262-1"><a href="#cite_note-USSmil-262">[262]</a></sup> The National Guard was delayed in reaching Saint John due to the number of overturned boats left in the harbor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup></p>
<p>At a September 10 news conference, Governor <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Mapp" title="Kenneth Mapp">Kenneth Mapp</a> described Irma as a "horrific disaster" for which "[t]here will be no restorations or solutions in days or weeks." The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> airlifted in goods for residents, who were subjected to a curfew. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_Cruise_Lines" title="Norwegian Cruise Lines">Norwegian Cruise Lines</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Caribbean_Cruise_Line" title="Royal Caribbean Cruise Line">Royal Caribbean Cruise Line</a> agreed to transport tourists to Florida, contingent upon port availability following the state's own experience with Irma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup></p>
<p>On Saint John, which was described by <i>The Washington Post</i> as "perhaps the site of Irma's worst devastation on American soil," it took six days for an active-theater disaster zone to be established, leading to criticism of the U.S. government response. The National Guard was brought in to maintain order, while the Coast Guard brought evacuees to cruise ships bound for <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> and Miami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
