<th rowspan="2">7</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">"Okeechobee"</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/1928_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1928 Atlantic hurricane season">1928</a></td>
<td align="center">929 mbar (hPa)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Irma</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">2017</a></td>
<td align="center">929 mbar (hPa)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th rowspan="2">9</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/1926_Miami_hurricane" title="1926 Miami hurricane">"Great Miami"</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/1926_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1926 Atlantic hurricane season">1926</a></td>
<td align="center">930 mbar (hPa)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Donna" title="Hurricane Donna">Donna</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/1960_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1960 Atlantic hurricane season">1960</a></td>
<td align="center">930 mbar (hPa)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th colspan="4"><small>Source: HURDAT,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_317-0"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-317">[317]</a></sup> Hurricane<br/>
Research Division<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_hurricanes_318-0"><a href="#cite_note-US_hurricanes-318">[318]</a></sup></small></th>
</tr>
</table>
<p>When Irma reached Category 5 intensity with winds of 175 mph (280 km/h) at 11:45 UTC on September 5 at 57.7°W,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-20">[20]</a></sup> it became the easternmost Atlantic hurricane of this strength on record, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_David" title="Hurricane David">Hurricane David</a> of <a href="/wiki/1979_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1979 Atlantic hurricane season">1979</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MDRstrength_319-0"><a href="#cite_note-MDRstrength-319">[319]</a></sup> By 00:15 UTC on September 6, Irma reached peak intensity with 185 mph (295 km/h) winds and a minimum <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">pressure</a> of 914 mbar (914 hPa; 27.0 inHg). This ties it as the second-strongest Atlantic hurricane by wind speed, surpassed only by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Allen" title="Hurricane Allen">Allen</a> of <a href="/wiki/1980_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1980 Atlantic hurricane season">1980</a> which reached wind speeds of 190 mph (305 km/h). Irma sustained these 185 mph (295 km/h) winds for 37 hours, becoming the only tropical cyclone worldwide to have had winds that speed for that long, breaking the previous record of 24 hours set by <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Haiyan" title="Typhoon Haiyan">Typhoon Haiyan</a> of <a href="/wiki/2013_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2013 Pacific typhoon season">2013</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colostate_320-0"><a href="#cite_note-colostate-320">[320]</a></sup> Only four other Atlantic hurricanes have been recorded with wind speeds of 185 mph (295 km/h) or higher: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Wilma</a> of <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1935_Labor_Day_hurricane" title="1935 Labor Day hurricane">1935 Labor Day hurricane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Allen" title="Hurricane Allen">Hurricane Allen</a> of <a href="/wiki/1980_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1980 Atlantic hurricane season">1980</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gilbert" title="Hurricane Gilbert">Hurricane Gilbert</a> of <a href="/wiki/1988_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1988 Atlantic hurricane season">1988</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> Upon reaching peak intensity, Irma also became the strongest hurricane ever recorded in the Atlantic basin outside the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup> as well as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">strongest Atlantic hurricane</a> since Wilma in terms of <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">maximum sustained winds</a>, and the most intense in terms of pressure since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dean" title="Hurricane Dean">Dean</a> in <a href="/wiki/2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2007 Atlantic hurricane season">2007</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSU_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-CSU-323">[323]</a></sup> In addition, Irma achieved one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Atlantic_hurricane_records#Longest_duration_as_a_Category_5_hurricane" title="List of Atlantic hurricane records">longest durations of Category 5 strength winds</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup> and the third-highest <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy#Individual_storms" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">accumulated cyclone energy</a> (ACE) index for a tropical cyclone in the Atlantic basin, with a value of 66.6 units. Only the <a href="/wiki/1899_San_Ciriaco_hurricane" title="1899 San Ciriaco hurricane">1899 San Ciriaco hurricane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">Hurricane Ivan</a> in 2004 achieved higher values.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCNOW_325-0"><a href="#cite_note-SCNOW-325">[325]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 6, Irma made landfall on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ginger_Island" title="Ginger Island">Ginger Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tortola" title="Tortola">Tortola</a> at peak strength. This made Irma the third-strongest tropical cyclone to make landfall globally – in terms of sustained winds – along with the 1935 Labor Day hurricane and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Typhoon_Joan_(1959)" title="Typhoon Joan (1959)">Typhoon Joan</a> of <a href="/wiki/1959_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="1959 Pacific typhoon season">1959</a>, trailing only typhoons Haiyan of <a href="/wiki/2013_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2013 Pacific typhoon season">2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Meranti" title="Typhoon Meranti">Meranti</a> of <a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2016 Pacific typhoon season">2016</a>, which bore winds of 195 mph (315 km/h) at landfall. Irma is tied with the <a href="/wiki/1935_Labor_Day_hurricane" title="1935 Labor Day hurricane">1935 Labor Day hurricane</a> as the strongest landfalling cyclone on record in the Atlantic basin, and is the first hurricane to make landfall anywhere in the Atlantic at Category 5 status since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Felix" title="Hurricane Felix">Felix</a> in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Landfallrecord_326-0"><a href="#cite_note-Landfallrecord-326">[326]</a></sup> Irma is the first recorded Category 5 hurricane to affect the northern <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a>, and was one of the worst storms to hit the region on record, along with <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Donna" title="Hurricane Donna">Hurricane Donna</a> in <a href="/wiki/1960_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1960 Atlantic hurricane season">1960</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Luis" title="Hurricane Luis">Hurricane Luis</a> in <a href="/wiki/1995_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1995 Atlantic hurricane season">1995</a>. In addition, Irma was only the second hurricane on record to make landfall in Cuba at Category 5 intensity, with the other being <a href="/wiki/1924_Cuba_hurricane" title="1924 Cuba hurricane">a hurricane in 1924</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSU_323-1"><a href="#cite_note-CSU-323">[323]</a></sup></p>
<p>Irma made landfall in the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a> with winds of 130 mph (215 km/h) and a pressure of 929 mbar (hPa; 27.43 inHg), making it the strongest hurricane to strike Florida in terms of windspeed since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Charley" title="Hurricane Charley">Charley</a> in <a href="/wiki/2004_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2004 Atlantic hurricane season">2004</a>, and the most intense to strike the state in terms of barometric pressure since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Andrew" title="Hurricane Andrew">Andrew</a> in <a href="/wiki/1992_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1992 Atlantic hurricane season">1992</a>. In the span of two weeks, two Category 4 hurricanes—<a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Harvey</a> and Irma—struck the continental United States, the first time on record two Atlantic tropical cyclones of such strength made landfall on the country in the same hurricane season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup> This also marked only the third occurrence of two consecutive Atlantic storms making landfall in the United States as major hurricanes. The other two instances were the <a href="/wiki/1893_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Nine" title="1893 Atlantic hurricane season">Great Charleston</a>/<a href="/wiki/1893_Cheniere_Caminada_hurricane" title="1893 Cheniere Caminada hurricane">Cheniere Caminada</a> hurricanes in <a href="/wiki/1893_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1893 Atlantic hurricane season">1893</a> and Hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">Ivan</a>/<a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jeanne" title="Hurricane Jeanne">Jeanne</a> in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCNOW_325-1"><a href="#cite_note-SCNOW-325">[325]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Irma&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">
<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="2004" data-file-width="3032" height="21" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Cyclone_Catarina_from_the_ISS_on_March_26_2004.JPG/32px-Cyclone_Catarina_from_the_ISS_on_March_26_2004.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Cyclone_Catarina_from_the_ISS_on_March_26_2004.JPG/48px-Cyclone_Catarina_from_the_ISS_on_March_26_2004.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Cyclone_Catarina_from_the_ISS_on_March_26_2004.JPG/64px-Cyclone_Catarina_from_the_ISS_on_March_26_2004.JPG 2x" width="32"/></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Tropical_cyclones" title="Portal:Tropical cyclones">Tropical cyclones portal</a></span></li>
<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="flag" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="21" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Flag_of_Florida.svg/32px-Flag_of_Florida.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Flag_of_Florida.svg/48px-Flag_of_Florida.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Flag_of_Florida.svg/64px-Flag_of_Florida.svg.png 2x" width="32"/></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Florida" title="Portal:Florida">Florida portal</a></span></li>
</ul>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes</a>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> (2017) – attained Category 5 status less than 2 weeks after Irma reached the same intensity, and impacted areas previously affected by Hurricanes Irma and Jose.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Matthew" title="Hurricane Matthew">Hurricane Matthew</a> (2016) – caused damage and deaths in Haiti, before moving to The Bahamas and then skimming the coastline of Florida, before moving up the coast.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">Hurricane Hugo</a> (1989) – also formed east of the Lesser Antilles, the easternmost known Category 5 hurricane in the Atlantic basin.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Andrew" title="Hurricane Andrew">Hurricane Andrew</a> (1992) – the last Category 5 hurricane to strike Florida.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1935_Labor_Day_hurricane" title="1935 Labor Day hurricane">"Labor Day"</a> (1935) – most intense hurricane to make landfall in the United States.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Hurricane Jose (2017)</a> – a Category 4 hurricane, which formed right behind Irma and also tracked into the Caribbean region.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Hurricane Harvey</a> (2017) – a Category 4 hurricane (and the first major one to make landfall in the U.S. in 12 years) which devastated Texas two weeks prior to Irma.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Luis" title="Hurricane Luis">Hurricane Luis</a> (1995) – very damaging and powerful hurricane that caused severe impacts in the northern Lesser Antilles.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Marilyn" title="Hurricane Marilyn">Hurricane Marilyn</a> (1995) – caused destruction as a rapidly intensifying hurricane in the northern Leeward Islands, which had been affected by Luis shortly beforehand.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Donna" title="Hurricane Donna">Hurricane Donna</a> (1960) – brushed the Lesser Antilles, before hitting the Florida Keys in early September at Category 4 intensity and travelling up the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast of the United States</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Operation_RUMAN" title="Operation RUMAN">Operation RUMAN</a> – UK military-civil disaster relief response to Hurricane Irma.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">1928 Okeechobee hurricane</a> – a hurricane that hit similar areas, for comparing tracking methods and after-effects with those of Hurricane Irma.</li>
</ul>
